<script>
  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }
    
    function initAppleId() {
      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',
        redirectURI: 'https://www.goodreads.com/apple_users/sign_in_with_apple_web',
        state: 'apple_oauth_state_2b20818f-2bc5-4146-92da-1a3c3c8353d0'
      });
    }
    
    var initializeSiwa = function() {
      var APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL =  "https://appleid.cdn-apple.com/appleauth/static/jsapi/appleid/1/en_US/appleid.auth.js"
      loadScript(APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL, initAppleId);
    };
    if (typeof AppleID !== "undefined") {
      initAppleId();
    } else {
      initializeSiwa();
    }

  <span id="freeText13032334291801200118" style="display:none">This book is permanently free on Amazon, BN.com, Apple, Kobo and more!<br /><br />Sora Fallcrest always dreamed of adventure, but as a member of the nobility, she learned the ways of a Lady instead. Now seventeen, she is expected to choose a husband and marry. She plots to run away, but just as she is stepping out the door, she runs into a mysterious man--and is kidnapped.<br /><br />Abducted from her manor, Sora is plunged into a world of magical races, arcane jewelry and forgotten lore. She finds herself at the mercy of a dangerous assassin, haunted by an even darker past. She yearns for freedom, but he won't let her go--not when her Cat's Eye necklace is the only thing that can save his life.<br /><br />But the necklace itself presents a problem. It is an ancient device from the long forgotten War of the Races, and its magic has the ability to steal souls. Can Sora learn to wield its power -- or will the power wield her? (Winner of the SKOW 2006 Best Fantasy Award)</span>

The plot isn't really complicated so I don't think that it should be a problem.. <br />So I would say that it would be for around 15/+ ;)<br /><br />P.S. : this answer isn't only for Sora's quest but also count for the other books:)<a class="jsHide hideAction" href="#">(less)</a></span></span>

<span id="freeTextContainer14739661897196879977"><img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1453374780i/17818041.jpg' width='130' height='30' alt='description' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/><b>FREE on Amazon!</b><br/><br/>I've been having a little trouble lately finding books that manage to keep me entertained throughout. I wouldn't exactly call it a book slump, but I've definitely been easier to please.<br/>Which is why I've been doing some re-reads of books I really enjoyed in the past, one of which is <i>Sora's Quest</i> by T.L. Shreffler, and I feel like I should finally do a review of it.<br/><br/>I really am not into High Fantasy. Stories of that genre have the tendency to be too abstract for my simple little mind</span>
  <span id="freeText14739661897196879977" style="display:none"><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1453374780i/17818041.jpg" width="130" height="30" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><b>FREE on Amazon!</b><br><br>I've been having a little trouble lately finding books that manage to keep me entertained throughout. I wouldn't exactly call it a book slump, but I've definitely been easier to please.<br>Which is why I've been doing some re-reads of books I really enjoyed in the past, one of which is <i>Sora's Quest</i> by T.L. Shreffler, and I feel like I should finally do a review of it.<br><br>I really am not into High Fantasy. Stories of that genre have the tendency to be too abstract for my simple little mind to follow and comprehend. Urban Fantasy I understand. I can relate. Epic Fantasy? Not so much, what with all those strange places and societies and names and creatures and stuff. <br>So color me surprised that I ended up really, really enjoying this one.<br><br>This is the story of Sora Fallcrest, a noble-born, sheltered girl who longs for adventure instead of being wed off to a stranger as a status symbol. What she doesn't bank on is being kidnapped on her 17th birthday by an assassin who is as ruthless as he is deadly, and ending up on the run both from authorities and a dangerous mage who has nothing left to lose.<br><br>I consider this book "Epic Fantasy <i>light</i>". There was some good world building, definitely enough to satisfy my needs, a fast-paced, well-wrought plot, very enjoyable characters (<a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[I miss, you, Dorian! *sigh* <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span>) and the slightest hint of romance that will be growing and evolving as the series progresses, but never be in the fore.<br>(Seriously, the romance is so slow-burn that even 70% into the book, Sora thinks this: <br><i>She put her hand to her chest, trying to calm her heart. He might be dead. The thought didn't truly upset her - but he was her only chance of survival.</i><br>And what can I say? I loved that the author didn't succumb to the ever-present insta-love cliché.)<br><br>Long story short: This is one hell of a series that deserves a lot more attention. You should read it. Really.</["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></span>

    <a title="T.M. Smith" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5041287-t-m-smith"><img alt="T.M. Smith" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1566755104p2/5041287.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/375509826?book_show_action=true">Jul 23, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="T.M. Smith" class="user" itemprop="url" name="T.M. Smith" href="/user/show/5041287-t-m-smith">T.M. Smith</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer375509826" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1566472633705610772">Let me start by saying, Cover LOVE! The story did not disappoint, I was jerked in from the first page and, before I knew it, I was screaming at my Kindle because I’d come to the end. The writing and the story are completely original and, although you’re just reading the story, it will seem as though you’ve been swept away and dropped into the middle of Sora’s world; Shreffler is just that good a writer. Her characters embody realism, depth and courage.<br/><br/>Crash (AKA Viper) stole the book for me thou</span>
  <span id="freeText1566472633705610772" style="display:none">Let me start by saying, Cover LOVE! The story did not disappoint, I was jerked in from the first page and, before I knew it, I was screaming at my Kindle because I’d come to the end. The writing and the story are completely original and, although you’re just reading the story, it will seem as though you’ve been swept away and dropped into the middle of Sora’s world; Shreffler is just that good a writer. Her characters embody realism, depth and courage.<br /><br />Crash (AKA Viper) stole the book for me though, a complete ass to the point of hating him in the beginning.. and yet, there is that mystery about him that makes you second guess your initial opinion of him. Sexy, brooding and secretive; I can’t wait to run into him again in book 2 (conveniently titled Viper’s Creed!). I thoroughly enjoyed watching the relationships between the characters as they developed and grew, leaving me in tears several times! Shreffler leaves us on the edge of a cliff, anxiously waiting to see what will happen with Sora and Crash. <br /><br />I do love a strong female character and Sora definitely delivers. She is young and unsure of herself to start but, she is determined to see her journey through to the end and becomes extremely loyal and protective of her 3 new friends by the end. <br /><br />I give this book 5/5 but, that’s just my two cents. <br /></span>

<div id="review_2681864603" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2681864603" />
    <a title="Lucie V." class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/84801697-lucie-v"><img alt="Lucie V." src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1597788485p2/84801697.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2681864603?book_show_action=true">Jan 24, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Lucie V." class="user" itemprop="url" name="Lucie V." href="/user/show/84801697-lucie-v">Lucie V.</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/34352236-sora-s-quest">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/84801697-lucie-v?shelf=will-not-read-again">will-not-read-again</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2681864603" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7790228554381175331">Well first of all… Free book on Amazon, why not? Let’s give it a try! Also, it doesn’t hurt that the story is about fantasy, magic, an assassin, and a runaway girl. The reviews were also quite good but honestly, I was disappointed. It was not a bad book, but it was not a good book either, I was expecting (hoping for) more.<br/><br/>The world-building was quite ordinary. We understand that there are humans and few other species (some with magic, some without...?), that there was a war between the humans an</span>
  <span id="freeText7790228554381175331" style="display:none">Well first of all… Free book on Amazon, why not? Let’s give it a try! Also, it doesn’t hurt that the story is about fantasy, magic, an assassin, and a runaway girl. The reviews were also quite good but honestly, I was disappointed. It was not a bad book, but it was not a good book either, I was expecting (hoping for) more.<br /><br />The world-building was quite ordinary. We understand that there are humans and few other species (some with magic, some without...?), that there was a war between the humans and the species, but other than that, it is hard to imagine what this world looks like. What is its history? How is it mapped? I need more details, all I kept imagining was a swamp and a jungle. There is blood magic, Earth magic, a king of wolf-fae species, were-cats…. Overall a lot of potential for a world-building, but it was not well exploited, nor was it developed enough.<br /><br />The characters were plain. Sora (the main character) was just painfully naive at times. She is also a bit hypocrite at the beginning of the story… Bitch-talking about the nobles while being exactly like them with her misplaced pride and belief that she’s safe just because she’s somebody’s daughter. It does get better as the book went on, but I did not like her at all, I just couldn’t get attached to her. Dorian was the only one that I found funny and grew attached to… A little bit.<br /><br />Finally, the story… I’m still not sure what the plot is supposed to be. There is a huge hatred between Crash and Volcrian because Crash killed Volcrian’s brother (a few years ago I would assume…). Volcrian is chasing Crash to get revenge and all Crash and his gang seems to be doing is fleeing and taking side criminal jobs to get money. They stumble upon Sora who conveniently has a magic necklace that can help them escape Volcrian and that’s it, she can be part of the crew, but they still need to escape and start anew someplace far away. That’s it. Nothing else. <br />The story was also quite fast-paced, but not in a bad way. The characters are in a hurry, but the evolution of their relationship is still ‘’ normal-paced ‘’, nobody magically falls in love after 3 days (I was a little afraid of a basic, rushed love story between Sora and one of the other characters, probably Crash).<br /><br />Overall it is an ''okay'' book if you can go through the first half. I’m still not sure if I will read the following book because although I was not impressed by the first half of the book, I must admit that the end was better and it lets me hope that maybe the second book will also be better…</span>
  <a data-text-id="7790228554381175331" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_717560494" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/717560494" />
    <a title="Ornella (Nyx)" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/6282007-ornella-nyx"><img alt="Ornella (Nyx)" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1363660589p2/6282007.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/717560494?book_show_action=true">Sep 11, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Ornella (Nyx)" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Ornella (Nyx)" href="/user/show/6282007-ornella-nyx">Ornella (Nyx)</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer717560494" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9714485943457155147">I guess you could say I had high expectations for this series. It's a fantasy, there is an assassin involved. I was sold from the get-go. The raving reviews just solidified my resolve to read this. I was expecting it to be awesome. It wasn't.<br/><br/>It wasn't bad, but I wanted <i>better</i>. Let me break it down so I can make it easier.<br/><br/>World-building (3.5/5): It wasn't as lush and detailed as it could be/wanted it to be, but it was more than decent enough. We get told of different races, the War of the Races, </span>
  <span id="freeText9714485943457155147" style="display:none">I guess you could say I had high expectations for this series. It's a fantasy, there is an assassin involved. I was sold from the get-go. The raving reviews just solidified my resolve to read this. I was expecting it to be awesome. It wasn't.<br /><br />It wasn't bad, but I wanted <i>better</i>. Let me break it down so I can make it easier.<br /><br />World-building (3.5/5): It wasn't as lush and detailed as it could be/wanted it to be, but it was more than decent enough. We get told of different races, the War of the Races, the destruction by the humans (Damn humans!) with the Cat's Eye. We get to meet some of them as well. 2 of our main characters are Wolfies (which is such a cute name!). They reminded me of a blend between Fae and werewolf. <br /><br />Our assassin, seems to be of a different race entirely and we only get bits and pieces of information about this race in general. I'm hoping for more in the next book. One of the conflicts that out characters go through is fighting the Catlins, which are these huge werecat type of race, that use Earth Magic. As I said, very nice world building, but it could have been exploited a lot more as well.<br /><br />Characters (2.5/5): Characters are huge for me, and for the life of me I could not like Sora at all. She got a bit more tolerable as the book went on, but just enough that I didn't finally give up on it. She would have single-handedly ruined the whole book for me. The only thing that kept me going and hoping that Sora would get better was the promise of the world-building, but I came SO close to just DNFing it because of her. <br /><br />She was so naive and plain stupid at times. She liked to think that she wasn't like those snobbish nobles from the City, but she was exactly like them. She was also irrational and I just don't handle irrational characters well. She had this forced hatred towards the men that made me want to strangle her! <br /><br />They treated her so damn well, even giving her weapons after only like 2 days of being 'kidnapped' and all she did was judge, bitch and whine the whole fucking time. If it had been some kind of plan, that she was masking her brilliance with this act, or getting on their nerves so they would tired of her and just dump her ass, I would have been all for it, but it wasn't! Ugh.<br /><br />With that said I liked the rest of our gang, Burn, Dorian and specially Crash, just being a badass assassin :)<br /><br />Plot (2/5): The plot seems too simple? Idk if I'm missing something but the basic thing is, Crash/Viper (the assassin) killed Volcrian's brother as an assignment. Volcrian vows revenge, fails the first time and the chase ensues. So all Crash and the rest of his party are doing is just running from Volcrian, while doing side jobs to keep the money going. That't it. That's the whole of the plot. There is no side issues going on that I can see. Just straightforward revenge.<br /><br />The pacing (4/5) was quite nice always a sense of urgency, suspense. Always being chased, or chasing. The romance (2/5) was well, idk. There wasn't much of anything really, which I appreciated, but we are getting weird vibes/feelings between Sora and Crash and I just don't think Sora is anywhere good enough for Crash, which is why I don't like where things are going.<br /><br />So overall it was an enjoyable enough fantasy once you get past the halfway mark (before that Sora was just too plain irritating to enjoy anything else). Would I recommend it? Idk. I'd have to finish the series to see if it was worth starting, but I think I might just find out. Still haven't made up my mind about reading the second book or not.</span>
  <a data-text-id="9714485943457155147" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_801894985" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/801894985" />
    <a title="Eli Hinze" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/6398504-eli-hinze"><img alt="Eli Hinze" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1489510521p2/6398504.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/801894985?book_show_action=true">Dec 27, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Eli Hinze" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Eli Hinze" href="/user/show/6398504-eli-hinze">Eli Hinze</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/16084685-sora-s-quest">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6398504-eli-hinze?shelf=2014-reading-list">2014-reading-list</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6398504-eli-hinze?shelf=2015-reading-list">2015-reading-list</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6398504-eli-hinze?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6398504-eli-hinze?shelf=indie">indie</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer801894985" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11920836777501682104"><br/>I have a weird relationship with this book. My affection for it is split along a very clear divide. There’s the first 80% of the book, which I’ll review in one chunk, and then the remaining 20%, which I will also review in its own separate chunk.<br/><br/>So, let’s take a look at the first 80%.<br/><br/>For the first 80% of the book I really wasn’t feeling it. It read more like a middle grade book to me. There’s absolutely nothing wrong with middle grade, but it just wasn’t what I was expecting. I didn’t feel a hug</span>
  <span id="freeText11920836777501682104" style="display:none"><br />I have a weird relationship with this book. My affection for it is split along a very clear divide. There’s the first 80% of the book, which I’ll review in one chunk, and then the remaining 20%, which I will also review in its own separate chunk.<br /><br />So, let’s take a look at the first 80%.<br /><br />For the first 80% of the book I really wasn’t feeling it. It read more like a middle grade book to me. There’s absolutely nothing wrong with middle grade, but it just wasn’t what I was expecting. I didn’t feel a huge connection with the characters, nor was I super interested in their dynamic with one another. (I did however like all the bits with Dorian though. He’s such a darling.) The writing was just okay at this point. It wasn’t anything spectacular, and to be honest a little cheesy in parts. The pacing had a major lull in the middle, as is sort of common in fantasy novels. Also common is the fantasy formula for generating plot which is “don’t know what to do next with your characters? Have them get attacked by a crazy monster!”. This gets very old vey fast when used in abundance, as it is here.<br /><br />Now, the remaining 20%.<br /><br />You may be wondering, then why the high rating? You see, I have no idea what happened in the last bit of the book, but the writing suddenly took on a new, astonishing quality. The pace was perfection. The character dynamics showed multiple layers, tantalizing and rich. The characters were infused with an indescribable vitality. I have to be honest, if I’d only read the first 80% I wouldn’t have been interested in reading the next book. The last 20% changed everything, and I’m very excited to read book number two!<br /><br />In conclusion, I would recommend this book. While I initially didn’t care for it, the ending part was just too compelling, too awesome to ignore. It has the promise of an exciting world to explore, authentic characters, and a plot that draws you in. If you’re a fan of fantasy far and wide, this is most definitely the book for you!</span>
  <a data-text-id="11920836777501682104" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1021225781" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1021225781" />
    <a title="Kalla [A Bookish Nerd]" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/26152762-kalla-a-bookish-nerd"><img alt="Kalla [A Bookish Nerd]" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1544527997p2/26152762.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1021225781?book_show_action=true">Aug 08, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Kalla [A Bookish Nerd]" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Kalla [A Bookish Nerd]" href="/user/show/26152762-kalla-a-bookish-nerd">Kalla [A Bookish Nerd]</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/16084685-sora-s-quest">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/26152762-kalla-a-bookish-nerd?shelf=ebooks">ebooks</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/26152762-kalla-a-bookish-nerd?shelf=fictional-boy-crush">fictional-boy-crush</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/26152762-kalla-a-bookish-nerd?shelf=kickass-mc">kickass-mc</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/26152762-kalla-a-bookish-nerd?shelf=love-love-love">love-love-love</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/26152762-kalla-a-bookish-nerd?shelf=i-ll-put-a-spell-on-you">i-ll-put-a-spell-on-you</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/26152762-kalla-a-bookish-nerd?shelf=the-usual-controlling-love-interest">the-usual-controlling-love-interest</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/26152762-kalla-a-bookish-nerd?shelf=young-adult-paranormal">young-adult-paranormal</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/26152762-kalla-a-bookish-nerd?shelf=multiple-pov">multiple-pov</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1021225781" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16061804156494122932"><b>I actually liked this.</b><br/><br/>I'll admit that I didn't have high expectations going into this book despite the raving reviews. I didn't like the cover despite the gorgeous girl. I didn't like the blurb, either, despite the fact that it wasn't horrendous. <i>I don't know what my problem was.</i> I just didn't think I would like it. <br/><br/>I was wrong. <br/><br/>The characters each had their own personalities that made them unique. The plot was easy enough to follow, but it was also very intricate. The time era in this book was </span>
  <span id="freeText16061804156494122932" style="display:none"><b>I actually liked this.</b><br /><br />I'll admit that I didn't have high expectations going into this book despite the raving reviews. I didn't like the cover despite the gorgeous girl. I didn't like the blurb, either, despite the fact that it wasn't horrendous. <i>I don't know what my problem was.</i> I just didn't think I would like it. <br /><br />I was wrong. <br /><br />The characters each had their own personalities that made them unique. The plot was easy enough to follow, but it was also very intricate. The time era in this book was very interesting; I liked it. The writing was not bad. I only saw a few minor grammatical errors. Needless to say, it was a fun read. <br /><br /><u>The MC is Sora.</u> (Does anyone think of Kingdom Hearts? No? Okay.) At the beginning of the book I saw her as more of a weak character. I thought that the author would portray her as this feeble, weak-minded lady that can't take care of herself for the entire book. However, Sora gets stronger. She transforms into this fierce and loyal young woman and <i>I totally respect that.</i> I am so thrilled that this isn't a book that suffers from Mary Sue. Sora is quick-witted, brash, and, at times, funny. She has a lot of crappy things going on in her life, sure, but that doesn't stop her from moving forward. I liked her a lot. <br /><br /><u>The other characters:</u> <b>Dorain.</b> I didn't think that I was going to like him considering he was a major douche at the beginning of the story, but I found my feelings toward him slowly change. In the end, I actually liked him. He was funny and sarcastic (which I love) but at the same time he was kind and caring. <b>Burn.</b> I felt the same way toward Burn that I did with Dorian. I didn't like him at all at first. He seemed sort of sneaky and sly- like he had other plans up his sleeve. He came off as someone I couldn't trust. Toward the end, though, I felt that start to change. I connected with him more. <b>Crash/Viper.</b> I definitely have mixed feelings about this assassin. He's definitely a douche. He's a jerk. He's cruel, rude, and he can be heartless. He's controlling and thinks that he's the person that should be making the orders. He doesn't care about anyone else's feelings or emotions. He only cares for himself. <i>I strongly disliked this part about him.</i> Even so, he begins to slowly evolve, slowly show his soft side. He begins to see the others as equals. He even has a loyal side to him. He's strong. He's a survivor. And, to a certain extent, I understand the reason why he's been such a jerk for most of the book. <i>He's an assassin. He's supposed to be rough.</i> He's built this rugged personality because he wants to live and he knows that if he doesn't he'll be dead. So, yeah, I get it. (But that doesn't mean I have to like it!) Anyway, I'm glad to see that he isn't just a cold killer. He does have feelings even though he keeps them hidden. <br /><br /><u>The plot.</u> It's easy enough to follow. In the book, you have Sora, Dorian, Crash, and Burn running from a blood mage who is hell bent on destroying them. The reader is introduced to many different settings- villages, swamps, etc. The story is not bland. It's evenly paced for the most part. I only found myself skimming a couple of pages. (Which is good considering I have the attention span of a bumblebee.) There's a lot of magic and fantasy in this book. If you like either of those, you might like this book. <br /><br /><u>The romance.</u> If you're into sappy romance with swoon-worthy lines full of lust and desire, this book is not for you. If you want an immediate connection or insta-love, this book is not for you. If you want a love triangle, this book is not for you. However, if you want a hatred-turned-friendship-that-might-evolve-into-something-more, this book is for you. The romance is very faint. This book focuses more on trust and friendship than anything else. Although, there might be a hint at romance to come for the sequel at the end of this book. <br /><br />Overall, I really liked this. It had a good balance of magic, friendship, the slow evolving of trust, and finding oneself. It was an entertaining read. There were a few (minor) plot twists toward the end of the book that I (sort of) didn't expect coming. I can think of one in particular. <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[Her mother... gosh, didn't expect it. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> <br /><br />There wasn't much that I didn't like about this book. The beginning was a little bit of a cliche to me. I felt that it was veering off into the "MC is stupid" land, but, luckily, that changed. <br /><br />My last thoughts? <i>I can't wait to read the sequel!</i> </span>
  <a data-text-id="16061804156494122932" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1016306373" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1016306373" />
    <a title="Kel" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3221228-kel"><img alt="Kel" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1401900820p2/3221228.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1016306373?book_show_action=true">Aug 04, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Kel" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Kel" href="/user/show/3221228-kel">Kel</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3221228-kel?shelf=pub-indie">pub-indie</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1016306373" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13781210039492737812"><i>Check out more reviews, discussions, lists and fan art at <a href='http://bookedtiltuesday.blogspot.com' rel='nofollow noopener'>Booked til Tuesday</a>.</i><br/><br/>My experiences with self-published works vary from good to bad to ugly. Luckily, this is one of the "good." I downloaded it to my Nook on a whim, read it during a crazy reading mood, and was pleased to find a good old fashioned fantasy adventure with danger, magic and killer cat people.<br/><br/><br/><b>What I Liked:</b><br/>I want more information on the world and the magic system, but I'm pretty happy with the little I've seen.<br/><br/>The characters gr</span>
  <span id="freeText13781210039492737812" style="display:none"><i>Check out more reviews, discussions, lists and fan art at <a href="http://bookedtiltuesday.blogspot.com" rel="nofollow noopener">Booked til Tuesday</a>.</i><br /><br />My experiences with self-published works vary from good to bad to ugly. Luckily, this is one of the "good." I downloaded it to my Nook on a whim, read it during a crazy reading mood, and was pleased to find a good old fashioned fantasy adventure with danger, magic and killer cat people.<br /><br /><br /><b>What I Liked:</b><br />I want more information on the world and the magic system, but I'm pretty happy with the little I've seen.<br /><br />The characters grew on me. Sora isn't one of my all-time favorite heroines, but she matures from a spoiled noble to a toughened trekker. A few sparring sessions does not a warrior make, but she's learning to take responsibility for herself and others and to work hard and purposely rush into danger. :) And the three traveling companions, while I would have liked to know them better, are decent. Of course, we are reading from Sora's perspective (in third person ^^), so we are limited by her thoughts and observations; but still, a cool little company.<br /><br />There is no romance, but there are hints that it may develop (very, very slowly) somewhere down the line.<br /><br />The ending could have been a complete letdown because the pages after the climax seemed to be winding down to a simple, "Bye, see you in the next book." But then the author did something really fun with it. No spoilers, but it was fun. :)<br /><br /><br /><b>What I Didn't Like:</b><br />The world is populated by humans and...others. The (nearly extinct) different races are a little...eh, almost stereotypical or cliched? Cat people, "Wolfies," some other to-be-named stuff, but at least they weren't all just humans with pointy ears. (Looking at you, Star Trek.) And the different types of magic they use are kind of cool.<br /><br />I want more details on the Cat's Eye magic (and other magic) and how it works.<br /><br />Volcrian, the main bad guy, was more creepy than scary to me. The blood sacrifices/magic and everything- creepy, yes, but I had a hard time believing our fierce band of warriors was running from him. Then again, he does have a tendency to conjure magical creatures that are near impossible to kill and bent on destroying the (anti)heroes.<br /><br /><br /><b>Final Thoughts:</b><br />I didn't fully realize this was self-published until after I'd finished it, but it read better than some of the small (and large) press books I've read recently, and I can't recall a single typo. When I get that kind of quality for free, I'm definitely more willing to spend a little on the sequels. (Which made me extra happy to catch Book 2, <i>Viper's Creed</i>, on sale for $0.99!)<br /><br />It's not the world's most amazing or original fantasy book, but the writing is pretty solid, it's not bogged down by the usual YA insta-love/love triangles, and it's free. Can't beat that, right? :)</span>
  <a data-text-id="13781210039492737812" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_319037580" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/319037580" />
    <a title="Gianne" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5761770-gianne"><img alt="Gianne" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1349839051p2/5761770.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/319037580?book_show_action=true">Apr 25, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Gianne" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Gianne" href="/user/show/5761770-gianne">Gianne</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer319037580" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12965711524129061441">Sora's Quest was such a fun read! During the whole time I was reading this, I felt like I was whisked away to a brand new world with endless possibilities of adventures and wonders.<br/><br/>I really liked the world building, especially the mythology and all the different races. I also loved the way how magic was perceived in this book, how it was mysterious and powerful and even dangerous. The only problem for me was that I wish there was more world building! I wanted to actually experience the different</span>
  <span id="freeText12965711524129061441" style="display:none">Sora's Quest was such a fun read! During the whole time I was reading this, I felt like I was whisked away to a brand new world with endless possibilities of adventures and wonders.<br /><br />I really liked the world building, especially the mythology and all the different races. I also loved the way how magic was perceived in this book, how it was mysterious and powerful and even dangerous. The only problem for me was that I wish there was more world building! I wanted to actually experience the different cultures each of these races had to offer and while reading this, I felt limited with what I was given.<br /><br />I also enjoyed the characters as well! My favorite out of all of them would probably be Crash. He's the most mysterious and even though he might have seemed like a total jerk at times, he had his moments. Dorian and Burn were also great, though I wished I could have seen more of Burn and both his and Dorian's back story. Last, but not least, we have our heroine, Sora! I couldn't help but be irritated at Sora sometimes because of her naivety but it wasn't her fault since she's been sheltered her entire life. However, she's a brave, strong heroine with admirable qualities like the courage to put her life before her friends. She may have her flaws, but she's a realistic kind of heroine which I adore.<br /><br />The plot was pretty interesting as well. Although not as many twists as I would have liked, I was constantly kept guessing at what would happen next! I couldn't stop turning the pages and I just ended up devouring the whole book.<br /><br />If there was something I wished I could have seen more in the plot, it would be romance. Good gosh, if you know me, you know I want, need, and crave romance! I'm not sure if Theresa intended there to be romance between our dark assassin and heroine, but I definitely felt just a bit of spark between the two. The slow build up between Sora and Crash was nice as they became from hostile strangers to friends who've shared memories together. Perhaps in the next book, their relationship will continue to grow and perhaps become something more. (Oh please, please, please, let it become something more!)<br /><br />The ending was completely bittersweet, with a couple of loose threads needed to tie up. Only very few of my questions were answered and I hope the rest of my questions will be answered in the next book. (Why must the sequel be in September? *sigh* I need more Crash and Sora time now.)<br /><br />Sora's Quest is a purely whimsical ride filled with enchanting adventures, witty banter between charming characters, and wonderful friendships (one with a possibility of romance) that will only grow even greater between our heroine and companions over the course of this series.</span>
  <a data-text-id="12965711524129061441" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1550246303" />
    <a title="Teigan" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/18664746-teigan"><img alt="Teigan" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1364096647p2/18664746.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1550246303?book_show_action=true">Dec 19, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Teigan" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Teigan" href="/user/show/18664746-teigan">Teigan</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1550246303" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10851875000956165127">4/4.5 stars.<br/><br/>This was <b>surprisingly good.</b><br/><br/><i>Sora's Quest</i> follows a band of misfit characters on a journey... my favourite type of story, speckled with a fantasy background. <br/><br/><b>Sora</b> is a second tier noblewoman, although without a place in high society as rumours swirl speculating on her legitimacy. <b>Crash</b> is an unfeeling assassin who knows his purpose and gets the job done. <b>Dorian</b>, cheeky and charismatic, the giver of comedic relief. And <b>Burn</b>, the mediator and giant teddy bear who I adored in their mini c</span>
  <span id="freeText10851875000956165127" style="display:none">4/4.5 stars.<br /><br />This was <b>surprisingly good.</b><br /><br /><i>Sora's Quest</i> follows a band of misfit characters on a journey... my favourite type of story, speckled with a fantasy background. <br /><br /><b>Sora</b> is a second tier noblewoman, although without a place in high society as rumours swirl speculating on her legitimacy. <b>Crash</b> is an unfeeling assassin who knows his purpose and gets the job done. <b>Dorian</b>, cheeky and charismatic, the giver of comedic relief. And <b>Burn</b>, the mediator and giant teddy bear who I adored in their mini cadre. <br /><br />When circumstances propel Sora into the paths of the three men, fear, dislike and hostility ensue. And somewhere along the way, loyalty, laughter... camaraderie? <br /><br />I love how smoothly the group dynamics changed. Each character began to reevaluate their preconceived notions of each other after each endurance the group experiences. The Stockholm Syndrome trope was entertaining as hell, but I would have been happier with another female character just to mix up the cast.<br /><br />The elements of fantasy and world building were easy to follow and explained succintly without leaving too many blanks. What I appreciated was that <b>Sora was completely mundane and anti-speshul-snowflake</b>-- she's clumsy, slightly spoilt and uncoordinated, but in a turn of events becomes the wielder of a Cat's Eye and forces her to accept the responsibility thrust upon her. She begins to learn to fight and develops beautifully into a believable blooming heroine. <br /><br />Crash and Sora are <u>PLAYING WITH MY HEARTSTRINGS.</u> The slow burn (pun unintended) is killing me and yet I fucking love that nothing has really started. The book promises a blossoming romance for the series, and <b>thank god for no insta-love</b> because I would have exploded in my review. <br /><br />Also I wasn't initially a big fan of the cover, but I've grown to like that it accurately depicts what was described in the book. <br /><br />While <i>Sora's Quest</i> had no elaborate plot and integrated the SS trope, <b>it deserves a high rating for being unadulturatedly enjoyable</b>, and I feel like that word is entirely underwhelming as a compliment to the book, but it's really that simple. I found myself compelled to keep reading in anticipation of what was to come and constantly bouncing with unsurpressed excitement. <br /><br />I'm so, so ready for the next book.</span>
  <a data-text-id="10851875000956165127" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1676470135" />
    <a title="The Captain" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/54489623-the-captain"><img alt="The Captain" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1459976325p2/54489623.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="The Captain" class="user" itemprop="url" name="The Captain" href="/user/show/54489623-the-captain">The Captain</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1676470135" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11722125910275043883">It is time to abandon ship me mateys!<br/><br/>I heard about this novel from Angela @ pooled ink who wrote a raving review. In fact, the review was so exuberant in its praise, that I immediately went and downloaded the novel, which was available for free on Amazon.<br/><br/>Now I had issues with this novel at the start. I didn’t like the prologue. But I thought to meself, “well, we are obviously not supposed to like the bad guy.” So I kept going. Then the novel proper started and we were introduced to the heroine.<br/><br/>T</span>
  <span id="freeText11722125910275043883" style="display:none">It is time to abandon ship me mateys!<br /><br />I heard about this novel from Angela @ pooled ink who wrote a raving review. In fact, the review was so exuberant in its praise, that I immediately went and downloaded the novel, which was available for free on Amazon.<br /><br />Now I had issues with this novel at the start. I didn’t like the prologue. But I thought to meself, “well, we are obviously not supposed to like the bad guy.” So I kept going. Then the novel proper started and we were introduced to the heroine.<br /><br />The main character Sora was a whiny brat of a 17 year old. Yes, her father is a bit of an unlovable jerk but she didn’t seem to have the worst life. I mean, I get that she doesn’t want to marry. I was cool with that. However, she didn’t seem to have any other plans except to run away. And how she went about it didn’t seem that bright.<br /><br />Now of course as she is attempting to run away, she is instead kidnapped by an assassin. I have a soft spot for assassin novels, so I got excited and thought that here is where it is going to start getting good.<br /><br />Sadly that was not true for me. New characters kept getting introduced and I didn’t like any of them. Not only that, but the world building seemed almost non-existent and flat. Add to the fact that the group wanders in the swamp in seemingly circles for the majority of the novel and I just couldn’t take it anymore.<br /><br />Now if I found the novel so irksome then why ye ask did I read to 79 percent? Because I somehow wanted to magically capture the reading enjoyment that Angela had. I mean, obviously she loved it and she quickly downloaded and gobbled up the remainder of the series. I kept thinking that if I kept reading the hook would catch me and the enthrallment would begin.<br /><br />But this seems to be a case of this novel not being for me. I had to abandon the book and subsequently the series.<br /><br />I am glad however that it has captured the fancy of other readers. So don’t necessarily take me word for it. Read the pooled ink’s contrasting viewpoint and if ye like to give this one a chance.<br /><br />As always I find when people disagree with me reading tastes to be sort of fascinating.<br /><br />If ye want to see me other reviews go to <a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="https://thecaptainsquartersblog.wordpress.com/">https://thecaptainsquartersblog.wordp...</a></span>

She once even mentioned that her father's death is almost trivial. 😱 <a class='jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction'>(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> She is so self-absorbed and whiny. I can't reca</span>
  <span id="freeText4896951661489899327" style="display:none"><a target="_blank" href="https://imageshack.com/i/pmUUSudig" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1500910324ra/23395024.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br>I once again find myself with an unpopular opinion. 😔 <br><br>Sora irks me to no end. I normally enjoyed reading about flawed heroine but nothing about her is likable. <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[ Sure, her father mostly ignore her but he is a good provider. She lives in comfort if not in luxury. I don't see how she can just leave her father that way without making sure he is safe. She once even mentioned that her father's death is almost trivial. 😱 <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> She is so self-absorbed and whiny. I can't recall if she ever spared a thought about her people. Being naive is one thing; not using common sense is another. She knows she is being interrogated for <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[ the murder of her father  <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> so what did she do? She provide motive for the said crime she is being accused. 🙄 She confirms the speculation. She is also a hypocrite <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[ hating the snobbish first tier while she is being a snob to those below her in rank.  <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> She is the definition of damsel-in-distress. She did improve on the last 4 chapters. She is almost like a different person. <br><br>Please don't get me started with the other characters. Crash/Viper had a sudden character growth on the last couple chapters that made me a little interested to check out the second book especially because it is titled after him. My favorite parts to read is the POV of the villain. 🙈 He is actually seem the only one to act rationally and being perfectly evil. 😉 <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[ but why didn't he use the wraiths sooner?  <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br><br><a target="_blank" href="https://imageshack.com/i/pmCOYP3wg" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1500910869ra/23395089.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br>The only thing I can count as positive is the slow burn romance. There is only very little romance (only a possibility of one for future installments). <br><br>The good news is the ebook version<br><a target="_blank" href="https://imageshack.com/i/pn3Wv4zbg" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1500910324ra/23395025.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br> 🎉 🎉Who knows? It might be a future favorite. I'm on the minority who doesn't like this book.</["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></span>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/501099405?book_show_action=true">Jan 09, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Kirsty (Amethyst Bookwyrm)" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Kirsty (Amethyst Bookwyrm)" href="/user/show/7436809-kirsty-amethyst-bookwyrm">Kirsty (Amethyst Bookwyrm)</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7436809-kirsty-amethyst-bookwyrm?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7436809-kirsty-amethyst-bookwyrm?shelf=review">review</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer501099405" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11510298999153357577">This and my other reviews can be found at <a target='_blank' rel='noopener nofollow' href='http://amethystbookwyrm.blogspot.co.uk/'>http://amethystbookwyrm.blogspot.co.uk/</a><br/><br/>Sora is not happy that her father is marrying her to a stranger, so she plans to run away. However before she can, her father is murdered and she is kidnaped by the assassin and a thief of a thought long extinct magical race called wolfies. However Sora is wearing a Cat’s Eye, a necklace that can protect her, which might help her complete her quest. <br/><br/>This is a YA fantasy book which is usually my favourite type of boo</span>
  <span id="freeText11510298999153357577" style="display:none">This and my other reviews can be found at <a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="http://amethystbookwyrm.blogspot.co.uk/">http://amethystbookwyrm.blogspot.co.uk/</a><br /><br />Sora is not happy that her father is marrying her to a stranger, so she plans to run away. However before she can, her father is murdered and she is kidnaped by the assassin and a thief of a thought long extinct magical race called wolfies. However Sora is wearing a Cat’s Eye, a necklace that can protect her, which might help her complete her quest. <br /><br />This is a YA fantasy book which is usually my favourite type of book but Sora’s Quest was just ok, because of the plot holes you just could not connect to much in this story. <br /><br />Sora is a very sheltered character who does know much about the outside world, but my main problem with her is that her thoughts make no sense, one second she hates Crash and next she is worrying about his safety. Also after a few days she seems to act like part of the group not a prisoner, which must be one of the quickest cases of Stockholm syndrome, which did not seem realistic. <br /><br /><a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[The main problem with this book is there are no motives for some of their actions. Firstly why does Sora want to go find her mother when she abandoned her, and yet did not care that her father was murdered just because he was distant even though he still looked after her. Secondly she never asks Crash why he killed her father and we never find out, also we don’t know why Crash killed Etienne, Volcrian’s brother. Also there was no reason why they kidnaped Sora as they did not know she had the Cat’s Eye. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br /><br />The one positive thing about this book is that it is very vivid and imaginative. Also it was nice to see some different races in fantasy books apart from elves, dwarfs etc. Overall Sora’s Quest is an average story that is let down by motives which do not make sense. </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1586209068" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16779808670303566586">Here is the book that got me obsessed with reading again! I've gone awhile without finding a series that I could really love. This is going on my favorite books ever shelf. I read all 4 books in 5 days because it was so danged good. <br/><br/>This book has a fantasy/paranormal feel to it. The main character (Sora) is a noble that wants to run away from her terrible father. Sora's father is murdered on the same night that she planned to run away. She ends up being kidnapped by the same person that murdered</span>
  <span id="freeText16779808670303566586" style="display:none">Here is the book that got me obsessed with reading again! I've gone awhile without finding a series that I could really love. This is going on my favorite books ever shelf. I read all 4 books in 5 days because it was so danged good. <br /><br />This book has a fantasy/paranormal feel to it. The main character (Sora) is a noble that wants to run away from her terrible father. Sora's father is murdered on the same night that she planned to run away. She ends up being kidnapped by the same person that murdered her father. The man is cruel and oddly inhuman. His companion isn't human at all and is what they call a "wolfy". The wolfy and the man have plans for Sora because they are on the run from a powerful wolfy mage. Sora is wearing a special necklace called a cats eye and the two kidnappers know that it can protect them. Sora is oblivious to the necklace but soon finds out that she is in for one crazy and terrifying adventure.<br /><br />The adventures found in these 4 books have been amazing. The characters were built up exactly the way I like them without the world building suffering at all. Everything was balanced. I just can't say enough about these books. You will find tons of magic and some very interesting characters. <br /><br />The first book is free on kindle and I'm pretty sure the author says it will always be free. Apparently the author knows that we will be hooked if we read the first book. The only bad thing is that the series isn't finished. There are 4 books so far.</span>

<div id="review_357687373" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/357687373" />
    <a title="Intisar Khanani" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/7924822-intisar-khanani"><img alt="Intisar Khanani" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1520258590p2/7924822.jpg" /></a>

    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/357687373?book_show_action=true">Jun 28, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Intisar Khanani" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Intisar Khanani" href="/user/show/7924822-intisar-khanani">Intisar Khanani</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer357687373" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4485188495389573174">**This is a review of the newly revised edition, released March 2013<br/><br/>About to be put on display to attract a suitor (i.e. the highest bidder), Sora decides to run away directly after her dance performance. Unfortunately for her, she's not the only one planning something: an assassin crashes the performance and kills her father. Fleeing in the ensuing chaos, Sora manages to escape the chaos, only to run into (quite literally) the assassin. Since he can't afford for her to blow his cover, he takes </span>
  <span id="freeText4485188495389573174" style="display:none">**This is a review of the newly revised edition, released March 2013<br /><br />About to be put on display to attract a suitor (i.e. the highest bidder), Sora decides to run away directly after her dance performance. Unfortunately for her, she's not the only one planning something: an assassin crashes the performance and kills her father. Fleeing in the ensuing chaos, Sora manages to escape the chaos, only to run into (quite literally) the assassin. Since he can't afford for her to blow his cover, he takes her with him. And things go from bad to worse. Including finding out she's psychically bound to the necklace her mother left her, a Cat's Eye with the power to eat magic...something the assassin could definitely use.<br /><br />Sora's quest is a fast-paced adventure story about a naive but strong-willed heroine who intends to set out into the world, only to have the world set upon her. This was a quick and engaging read to the point that it was almost over too fast! Sora develops well as a character, and Shreffler has spent a good amount of time building the world and its mythos. The supporting characters were well rounded and realistic, and there were a number of unexpected twists. I have confidence that, as Shreffler develops as a writer, her work will only get more interesting. This is definitely a writer I'll be watching. </span>
  <a data-text-id="4485188495389573174" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

I immensely enjoyed the adventure (oh, how I missed reading books like this!) and totally had a hard time putting the book down. <div id="review_426955089" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/426955089" />
    <a title="Kyra (Blog of a Bookaholic)" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/8844269-kyra-blog-of-a-bookaholic"><img alt="Kyra (Blog of a Bookaholic)" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1489267124p2/8844269.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/426955089?book_show_action=true">Oct 03, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Kyra (Blog of a Bookaholic)" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Kyra (Blog of a Bookaholic)" href="/user/show/8844269-kyra-blog-of-a-bookaholic">Kyra (Blog of a Bookaholic)</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer426955089" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3311383781742729960">Sora's Quest is one of the very few books I've read where my thoughts on it changed dramatically throughout the book. The beginning hooked me and had promise but as the book continued it lost me a bit. At one part it reminded me a bit of The Day of First Sun, a novel that I really didn't enjoy, however, I'm really happy I didn't give up on Sora's Quest as in the end I really enjoyed it.<br/><br/>What I liked about Sora's Quest as that I was immediately catapulted into the action. The first couple of chapt</span>
  <span id="freeText3311383781742729960" style="display:none">Sora's Quest is one of the very few books I've read where my thoughts on it changed dramatically throughout the book. The beginning hooked me and had promise but as the book continued it lost me a bit. At one part it reminded me a bit of The Day of First Sun, a novel that I really didn't enjoy, however, I'm really happy I didn't give up on Sora's Quest as in the end I really enjoyed it.<br /><br />What I liked about Sora's Quest as that I was immediately catapulted into the action. The first couple of chapters are of Sora getting ready to be married to a man that she has never met before, to whom her cold, distant father had arranged for her. She then plans on running away but as her father is about to make a toast and begin the wedding, a dagger whizzes out of no where, embedding itself in his throat. With her father murdered, Sora tried to make an escape but in the process she is kidnapped by the assassin and whisked away. The first couple of chapters the pace moved quite fast and it was a guessing game, as it was in third person (you know I don't like books written in third person? Well the author really made it work!) I didn't know if the assassin would kill her, what they wanted with her and where they were going. There were hundreds of questions flitting through my head and I was hungry for answers. As I kept on reading the questions were easily answered and I was quite satisfied.<br /><br />I liked the characters in the book. They all seemed to have depth to me and reasons for their actions. I wasn't actually too crazy about Sora when I was first introduced to her. When she saw her father murdered she didn't mourn at all and even though they barely communicated surely you would have some emotional reaction to seeing your father die in front of you? As I kept reading about her my liking grew for her. She really went through a change throughout the story, maturing. She was a brave, admirable heroine and she went from a spoilt brat to an adventurous warrior in a short space of time. It couldn't have been easy going from such a rich, luxurious life style to being a traveller and sleeping on the ground and hunting for your own food, I really think she adjusted well.<br /><br />My favourite character had to be all three of the original travellers though. Sora's relationship with Dorian, Burn and Crash was unique. I felt the bond she held with Dorian and Burn and I loved watching them interact with her and that she was melting their hearts one by one. I loved watching the spark that was beginning to ignite between Crash and Sora. There wasn't really romance in Sora's Quest which was a bit surprising seeing as its a YA book, but I have a feeling that Crash and Sora are going fall in love in the second instalment, Viper's Creed.<br /><br />Dorian, Burn and Crash were great characters. I really got to know the two Wolfies and I was extremely upset about what happened near the end. I like Crash but I hope to see more of his sensitive side in the second book, I think I'll like him even more in the next book. The couple of moments he showed sensitivity and human-like emotions to Sora really made my heart swell and I just felt a surge of love towards him.<br /><br />I only had a couple of issues with Sora's Quest. One of things is a couple of plot holes. There wasn't a clear reason for why Crash kidnapped Sora and that other major plot quirk that irked me a bit was their uneccessary journey through the swamp. The scenes that happened in the swamp were really detailed and jammed pack of action but there was no main reason for them to travel through the swamp. The other thing is that Sora's Quest didn't always hold my attention, there were times where I was finding myself not really interested in reading the book, so I hope in Viepr's Creed the author will write more jam-packed scenes.<br /><br />Overall, Sora's Quest was an interesting, entertaining novel. I loved watching Sora mature throughout the book and how her and the other characters relationships developed. There were quite a few twists in the tale that I hadn't expected at all! If you're a fan of magical books with beautiful description, then Sora's Quest will be right up your street. I think the author is very talented and I eagerly await Sora's second adventure.<br /><br />I give it: 3/5 CUPCAKES</span>
  <a data-text-id="3311383781742729960" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_368225101" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/368225101" />
    <a title="G33z3r" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/7136749-g33z3r"><img alt="G33z3r" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1402613612p2/7136749.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/368225101?book_show_action=true">Jul 14, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="G33z3r" class="user" itemprop="url" name="G33z3r" href="/user/show/7136749-g33z3r">G33z3r</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7136749-g33z3r?shelf=sword-sorcery">sword-sorcery</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7136749-g33z3r?shelf=ebook">ebook</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7136749-g33z3r?shelf=y-a">y-a</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer368225101" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17287026970496423397">"Sora's Quest" is a sword and sorcery fantasy novel for young adults set in a traditional pseudo-medieval fantasy world. The title character, Sora isn't thrilled with the marriage her noble father has arranged for her to a lord she's never met, and she's considering running away from home (thus abandoning her wealth and status.) Before she can act, her father is assassinated and she's kidnapped by one of the perpetrators. Soon, she is traveling with a trio of rough criminals (though there's no s</span>
  <span id="freeText17287026970496423397" style="display:none">"Sora's Quest" is a sword and sorcery fantasy novel for young adults set in a traditional pseudo-medieval fantasy world. The title character, Sora isn't thrilled with the marriage her noble father has arranged for her to a lord she's never met, and she's considering running away from home (thus abandoning her wealth and status.) Before she can act, her father is assassinated and she's kidnapped by one of the perpetrators. Soon, she is traveling with a trio of rough criminals (though there's no sense of peril in that abduction). Thus begins Sora's journey of adventure.<br /><br />"Sora's Quest" is a well paced action story, generally well written in the traditional fantasy style, and it's paced to never drag. The fantasy world it creates isn't far from the generic, but it offers a few twists on the usual sword &amp; sorcery realm of castles and magical artifacts, mostly in some new races. The tone is a little inconsistent, generally serious but with a light touch, except when it descends into outright farce in the portrayal of the jilted groom as an unbelievably self-centered fop ("Well, the bride's been kidnapped and her father murdered, but there's no sense wasting the reception banquet, is there? Let's party!) Fortunately, he isn't around for long.<br /><br />The story is woefully short on motive and reasons, though. I found it hard to accept Sora's total indifference to the murder of her father, an apparently decent man who raised her in luxury after her mother abandoned her, and who has no obvious vices beyond apparently not being loving enough and arranging her unwanted marriage. Yet, Sora doesn't shed a tear or even pause for long. It's never explained why he's murdered, and through all her travels with the assassin, Sora never even asks. It's not really clear why she's kidnapped in the first place, or why the criminals keep her around before they find out she bears a magical Catseye (an enchanted legacy apparently from her unknown mother. Once they know she wields its magic, they find her very useful.)<br /><br />Nor do we know where these three men are going or why they insist on taking such a dangerous route through a cursed swamp (what would they have done if they hadn't accidentally met someone with a Catseye to protect them from the curse? If it's a shortcut, why do they dawdle for over a month after crossing it?)<br /><br />By the halfway point of the novel, the journey becomes more one of survival than destination, which masks the total lack of purpose behind any of these events. But, when the dust clears at the denouement, that hollowness remains. <br /><br />As an elderly male, I'm certainly not the target audience for this, which seems aimed at teenage girls. As I said, the book is well-written and evenly paced. Presumably that target audience would find the adventure and promise of romance (small as it is) far more compelling than I.</span>
  <a data-text-id="17287026970496423397" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>
